The Shanghai County Education Bureau has formulated the following social education supervision methods: (1) The Bureau has formulated the supervision methods to improve the efficiency of social education. (2) In addition to the supervisors and education committee members conducting inspections in rotation according to regulations, the Bureau may send personnel to supervise various institutions at any time. (3) All public and private social education institutions in the county are within the scope of supervision. (4) Supervision matters: A. Internal aspects: 1. Organizational system, 2. Financial allocation, 3. Overview of operations, 4. Work plan, 5. Staff service, 6. Activities. B. External aspects: 1. People's lives, 2. Production organization, 3. Consumption, 4. Public utilities, 5. Cultural environment, 6. Social consciousness. (5) Supervision methods: A. Use the items mentioned in the social education supervision plan to create a table for use. B. Conduct on-the-spot investigations and interviews on the business and activity scope of the social education institutions. (6) At the end of each inspection, social education supervisors will evaluate the quality and compile a report to be submitted to the Bureau for review and award or punishment. (7) These methods will be submitted to the Provincial Department of Education for record-keeping and implementation.

County District Primary School Building Repair Methods 156

▲Schools Must Report Before August 31

▲Repair Work Managed by District Offices

The Shanghai County Education Bureau issued an order yesterday to the primary schools in the county's districts, stating: "Upon reviewing the 205th Bureau Affairs Meeting's discussion on the school building repair project in each district, it was decided that the repair project will be entrusted to the district offices based on the allocated funds for each district in the 20th-year budget. Because the funds allocated to each school for the temporary compulsory education are minimal, we are deeply concerned that annual repairs cannot be carried out school by school. It is necessary to prioritize urgent needs and carry them out in rotation. However, some schools may be unclear about this matter and have incorporated these funds into the equipment procurement fees and submitted them for approval. Now, it has been decided in the 211th Bureau Preliminary Meeting to issue a notice to all schools to list all items that need to be repaired and provide a budget, and submit them to the Education Committee before August 31st, without any delay. The Education Committee will submit a report based on the principal's report, referring to the actual situation of the inspection, and add their comments. The Bureau will send a letter to entrust the district offices to manage the repair work. In accordance with the above, in addition to informing the district offices, this order is for the principals to review and comply with. This order."

Special Report

Shanghai Municipal Bureau of Education's Vocational Facilities Plan for Secondary Schools This Year 171

The Shanghai Tianling Company Radio Station, to allow citizens to understand Shanghai's municipal plans, requested and was approved by the Municipal Government to have each bureau take turns sending personnel to broadcast lectures. The day before yesterday, it was the Municipal Bureau of Education's turn to broadcast, and Director Xu Peihuang sent Hu Shuyi to deliver a lecture on this topic. The reporter believes that production education is an urgent need for today's society, and hereby reveals it for the research of those concerned about education in this city. (Editor's note)

Brothers, today I represent the Shanghai Municipal Bureau of Education to lecture on the bureau's vocational facilities plan for secondary schools in the 20th year of the Republic. This lecture is prepared to be divided into three major parts. First, I will talk about the purpose of vocational facilities in the city's secondary schools. Second, I will talk about the plan to add vocational groups to the city's three secondary schools. Finally, I will talk about the bureau's relationship to promoting production education.

Now, let's first establish the purpose of vocational facilities in the city's secondary schools. Everyone understands that education is not the ultimate goal; it can only be said to be a tool for solving the problems that people need to solve. What problems does our country urgently need to solve now? I can briefly say it:

We now feel that society is uneasy and people's hearts are unsettled, mostly due to economic relations. In other words, it is the livelihood issue advocated by our President Sun Yat-sen. If it is not adequately resolved, then in this economically backward situation in China, if we want to save the people, save society, and save the country through education, we must change the original purpose of running education. We know that in the decades of running schools in our country, very few people in society have directly benefited because the schools do not consider the needs of society, and those who run education do not try to meet the needs of society. Therefore, the education sector has created a special class, and the result is that education is education and society is society. In that kind of situation, schools will become marketplaces for selling empty knowledge, and students, at best, will become impractical idealists. The activities in the school will be biased towards the mental aspect, and the activities of manual labor will never be dreamed of. Especially in our country's secondary schools, some people say that once young people enter secondary school, two phenomena will occur. First, they cannot operate. Second, they are unwilling to work hard. Therefore, students who enter secondary school are determined not to go to stores as apprentices, and female secondary school graduates are unwilling to operate at home. Do you think that society now needs this kind of talent who cannot operate and is unwilling to work hard? Therefore, many stores dare not hire secondary school graduates when hiring staff anymore. In the future, their only way out is to go to university; other than that, they are only qualified to be high-level idlers. This is the biggest weakness of current secondary education: there is no meaning of labor and vocational training. This weakness can also be said to violate our President Sun Yat-sen's advocacy of the omnipotence of hands. In the future, if every secondary school student becomes incapable, what hope is there for society and the country at that time? Because the various elements that make up society and the country are all dividing profits instead of creating profits. Now, to remedy this weakness, we must recognize where the needs of our society are and work together towards production-oriented education. Then, perhaps there is still some final hope. The bureau, recognizing this social need, is doing its best to promote production education in the secondary education stage, so that the citizens of Shanghai will receive vocational training in diligence and operation in the future and slowly embark on the path of production. This is the purpose of vocational facilities in the city's secondary schools. (To be continued)

Free Talk

World Snippets 172

— Hai Ke

Books in the British Museum

The British Museum, located in Europe, is prestigious. The British Museum is the largest museum in England. Taking only the library section as an example, it has a collection of three million books. If the bookshelves were laid flat on the ground and extended, they would be approximately thirty-five miles long.

A Country with Many Laws

The United States is a country with many laws. They have more than two million types of laws in effect. The most interesting one is a law passed in a certain town in Michigan in December 1923 that prohibits men and women from making eye contact with each other while dancing in public places. Contact is considered a violation of the law. However, this is the easiest thing to violate, and many people have been fined. In addition, in the parliament of a certain southwestern state, it was stipulated that women are prohibited from using powder. Also, in the state of Oklahoma, teaching the development of men and women is a crime. These laws are too strict and almost go too far.

Weihaiwei, Regaining Our Territory 173

— Feng

In recent years, the more satisfactory of our country's diplomatic negotiations has been the recovery of leased territories, and Qingdao and Weihai are examples of implementing the handover. Weihai's terrain is dangerous, controlling the Bohai Sea, and is an important military town for our country's maritime defense. Since its formal recovery, the government has designated it as an administrative district and established an administrative office. Xu Zushan was appointed as the commissioner. Mr. Xu is both talented in literature and martial arts and is familiar with diplomacy. Since taking office, he has been diligent in governing and making reforms in many ways. Local public security is well-organized, and people can leave their doors unlocked at night. Even though the British are nearby, there are no complaints. The climate is cool, and the scenery is extremely beautiful. It combines the advantages of both Putuo and Mogan Mountains and is the best area to live in and spend the summer. In the central part of the city, Mount Naigu is behind it. At the foot of the mountain is Huan Cui Lou (Green Ring Tower), which is the best place in the county. On clear spring and summer days, you can climb up to watch the sea and occasionally see mirages. However, the building has been around for many years and is gradually collapsing. Now, Commissioner Xu has rebuilt it. From then on, the famous tower and scenic spot will last forever. Once the project is completed, Mr. Zong will write about it specifically, which is also the history of the evolution of Weihai. Therefore, it is recorded to share with readers.

In the spring of the following year after I governed Weihai, I planted trees at the foot of Mount Naigu in the city and then ascended what is called Huan Cui Lou. I saw that it was backed by mountains, surrounded by hills, hanging upside down in the air, and densely populated by thousands of families. The floating scenery seemed boundless. Opposite was Liugong Island, with its solitary peak towering and supporting the middle of the river. The sea surrounded it on three sides, and Liugong Island acted as a screen. It was indeed a natural scenic spot and a strategic area for maritime defense. Looking back at the tower, the blackness of the rotten beams and rafters and the broken tiles were all bare and uneven. It had been abandoned and unrepaired for many years. Leaning on the railing and looking out, I was suddenly saddened. According to the records, the establishment of Weihaiwei was in the late Hongwu period of the Ming Dynasty to defend against pirates. During the Yongle period, the city was first built. Later, the city walls collapsed, and Zhao Heling, the deputy envoy of the patrol waterway, rebuilt it. Commander Wang Heng was grateful for Zhao's virtue and donated his salary to build Huan Cui Lou to show its permanence. Grand Secretary Liu was the one who wrote the inscription for it. It was rebuilt during the Shunzhi period of the Qing Dynasty. It collapsed in the forty-seventh year of Kangxi and was rebuilt in the first year of Qianlong. The records of the Weizhi (Weihai Gazetteer) describe the beginning and end of the tower in this way. Since the establishment of Weihaiwei in the early Ming Dynasty to defend against Japan, they knew that there was preparation in the northeast, so they changed their strategy of aggression and disturbed our Fujian and Yue borders. In the middle of the Guangxu period, Li Hongzhang supervised Zhili and opened Weihai as a military port, establishing a naval admiral to be stationed on Liugong Island. During the Sino-Japanese War, the Japanese surprised us. On one side, they attacked from Liaodong, and on the other side, they secretly landed from Chengshan, occupying our Weihai. The navy retreated to a place with no defense. Commander Deng Shichang was defeated and died in battle, and Admiral Ding Ruchang committed suicide by poisoning himself. As a result, our northeastern barrier was completely lost. Weihaiwei Bay almost became Japanese territory. The Qing court endured humiliation and made peace, ceding Taiwan and demanding Weihai back. In less than three years, the British forcibly leased it as a base for their navy in China. Counting from the 24th year of Guangxu in the former Qing Dynasty to the return in the 19th year of the Republic of China, Weihaiwei was a foreign land for a total of thirty-two years. I was ordered by the central government to guard this country. Tracing back from the early Ming Dynasty to the present, Weihai has had a dedicated city and official for six hundred years, and Huan Cui Lou, which stands high on the mountain, has been a scenic spot in Weihaiwei for almost five hundred years. Now, it is dilapidated and unrepaired, and it is about to collapse. It seems like Bao Mingyuan's "Ode to the Wasteland City." Will it make the scenic spots of one side be buried in the wilderness? This is the misfortune of the building, and it is also the insensitivity of the guard of the territory. Therefore, in July of this year, I ordered materials and construction workers to be hired. The project was completed in three months. In the central hall of the building, Zhao Heling was originally enshrined. Now, wooden tablets of Ding Ruchang and Deng Shichang are added. The project is about to come to an end. It happened that thousands of overseas Chinese in Korea were brutally massacred. Those who escaped took boats back to Weihai. The whole country was grief-stricken, and the hatred of the enemy was the same. I have been in the navy for a long time and have recently received special orders. Looking up and down, I feel even more sad. Since the opening of the sea ban, the great powers have surrounded us, gradually invading along the river and the sea, and it is not only Weihai. Taking Weihai as an example, it was originally intended to defend against Japan, but it was occupied by Japan, and then it was leased by the British. Now, although it has been separated from other ethnic groups and recovered its homeland, looking east to Lushun and the Korean Peninsula, I am saddened by the events of the Sino-Japanese War. The spirits of our naval martyrs in heaven are still difficult to rest in peace. Now, we have repaired it and added Ding and Deng to show our praise of the past and worship of the loyal and martyrs. Those who come later should also be responsible for defending against pirates and avenging the national humiliation. The sea and sky are boundless, and I look at it. If you say that you love the beauty of the forests and mountains and only use it for sightseeing, then how can it be my intention to repair this building? This is the record.

A Trip to the Temple of Li Bai 175

— Zhang Yan

In the sweltering summer, I went with my friend Sun Fangzhai to visit the Temple of Li Bai and returned. Therefore, this record is made and also tells those who have a penchant for landscapes.

Scholar Li Qinglian of the Tang Dynasty was drunk and jumped into the river to catch the moon while visiting Caishi at night and never returned. Later, it was said that he rode a whale to heaven. Although it is a myth, the relics still remain in the human world. Caishi belongs to Dangtu County, Taiping Prefecture, Anhui Province. It faces the Yangtze River and has a rocky head protruding from the river surface, which is quite dangerous and was also a place that ancient strategists had to contend for. There is Mount Cuiluo on the reef, with many scenic spots, such as the Ranxi Pavilion, where Wen Jiao of the Jin Dynasty burned rhinoceros horns. There are still the Eyebrow Pavilion, the Sanqing Temple, the Sanguan Cave, and the special temples of Peng, Yang, and Li, three famous ministers of the Qing Restoration. The most famous is the Temple of Li Bai. The temple has been built for a long time and was rebuilt during the Chenghua period of the Ming Dynasty. Later, it was renovated with the special temples of Peng and Yang, with the beauty of painted beams and carved pillars. The main hall enshrines the seated statue of Li Bai. The statue looks pure and strange, with long whiskers fluttering. He wears a green robe and a blue towel. In front of him is the Zhexian Tower, which was inscribed by former President Tan and is engraved with a reclining statue of Li Bai, with a glass in his hand, with the idea of raising a glass to invite the bright moon. Two children are serving by his side, one holding a sword and the other holding a pot, which is natural. It is said that this statue was made by a famous master, so it can look lifelike. Peng Xueqin of the Qing Dynasty had a couplet that said, "Don't write poems here. Who can be the enemy of a scholar?" "I often catch the moon in the river. I am willing to worship the wine fairy." Every time I visit a scenic spot, ordinary people always use vulgar pens to scribble, which spoils the scenery. Therefore, there is a vulgar saying that farting on a high wall is ridiculed. However, the pink walls in the Temple of Li Bai are as new, and there is no vulgar pen to stain them. Is it because I am showing off my slight skills and dare not write poems? It is strange. At the foot of Mount Cuiluo is the Qinglian Cemetery, which was established during the Daoguang period of the Qing Dynasty. It is now a school playground and is trampled on by people, which is only used for nostalgia. Caishi is ninety miles away from the capital by water. Small boats can reach it in all seasons, which is very convenient for tourists.

Talking About Police Dogs 176

— Qiushui

In the police stations of European countries, there are often trained dogs used to help the police investigate criminals and find murder weapons. For decades, the results have been excellent.

▲ One Policeman and One Dog: For example, in a murder case, the first step in the investigation is to find the murder weapon. At the same time, the murderer often anticipates this and will try to destroy the murder weapon or carry it to a distant place after the murder. The search for the murder weapon is therefore greatly difficult. However, if you have a skilled police dog, it will smell the scent and follow the trail. Soon after, it can be found without error. The great use of police dogs can be seen from this. Also, when a police officer walks alone on patrol at night or stands guard alone, a police dog is especially indispensable. Dogs are brave and loyal. If they encounter a strong thief, they will not be afraid even if they are faced with a pistol. Having a dog is like having three or four companions. Recently, many police dog experts in England held a meeting at "Crystal Palace" and decided to propose to the government that they should vigorously promote police dogs, so that every police officer in the country has a police dog.

▲ Special Good Dogs: However, the so-called police dogs must undergo long-term rigorous training before they can be put into practical use. And not just any ordinary dog can be used as a police dog. The current European countries use a special good product called "Alsatian." It is said to be the best kind. The temperament and physique of Alsatian police dogs are indeed more brave and strong than other dogs, and they also have the habit of only following one person and not eating if they are not fed by the owner. It is more suitable for the qualifications of police dogs. As long as you have lived with it for a long time, it will only recognize you in its mind and will follow you for life and will not go elsewhere. As long as you have regular daily feeding, it will not eat anything given to it by others. Police dogs, like police officers, will inevitably have many enemies over time. With this habit, you can absolutely avoid others poisoning it. And it has a very strong memory. Even if you take it to another place by train, it can find its way back home without getting lost. In addition to the Alsatian, there is another kind called "Great Dane," which is also very qualified to be a police dog. "Great Dane" was discovered by the British dog breeding expert Stewart and has recently been engaged in breeding. It is expected that in the near future, there will be more police dogs in the world.

Advice for Disaster Relief 177

— Chen Yien

When Louis XVI of France was about to ascend the guillotine, he laughed wildly. When Jin Shengtan was about to be executed, he chanted his poems loudly. Why? Because after these few minutes, there would be no more opportunities to laugh and chant. It can also be used to spend this moment of ten thousand arrows piercing the heart.

Today's victims in various places may not all be drowned to death. They are weeping silently, crying and jumping, like prisoners awaiting execution. How miserable are they? Alas, natural and man-made disasters occur suddenly. When they happen to you, you can only persevere in the ambition and knowledge of "the more chaotic things are, the more calm you must be" to deal with them. Otherwise, you will be at a loss and the misery will be doubled.

People in disasters will not be able to get everything they need in terms of clothing, food, housing, and transportation. Because they feel deeply inadequate in clothing, food, housing, and transportation, they are not calm in dealing with things, which will damage their spirit, disrupt their thinking, and weaken their physical strength. Even if natural and man-made disasters are not enough to kill me, I will also fall into suicide. Taking floods as an example, victims have nothing to rely on in terms of clothing, food, housing, and transportation. At this time, natural and man-made disasters such as lightning, storms, heavy rain, scorching sun, military mutinies, bandit robberies, and械斗 will come together. Rats and insects will bite and hurt. People are unfortunate enough to encounter this situation. Not only should they imitate Jin Shengtan and Louis XVI's wild chants and laughter at the time of disaster to relieve their own sorrow and stop the tears of others, but also calmly and bravely seek a way out. Clothing, food, and housing must also be considered according to one's ability. It is necessary to strive for more comfort and warmth than on a comfortable day. Otherwise, natural and man-made disasters can be escaped, but plagues and瘟神 will come. It's really inescapable. My saying this is not unreasonable. There is no end to the suffering. Disaster and disaster relief people, please pay attention.

Anecdotes About Kang Youwei 178

— Ms. Mei Su

I previously read an article by a gentleman in the Free Talk titled "Kang Youwei's Seal." I found it very interesting, so I remembered a small anecdote about Kang that my family member once mentioned. Therefore, I recorded it for the reader's amusement.

Decades ago, whenever people talked about Liang Weizhi of Guangdong, everyone knew that he was the wealthiest overseas Chinese in Kobe, Japan. The cost of marrying his daughter-in-law was no less than hundreds of thousands of gold. The former Japanese Emperor Taisho happened to be visiting Kobe at that time and heard that he was also a guest at the banquet. Kang was in exile in Japan at that time due to political affairs. On this day, he was also among the honored guests. After the banquet, it was customary to make a fuss in the bridal chamber. The guests all pushed Kang to come up with a question. Kang said that he was not good at this, but he heard that the bride had the reputation of a talented woman. Why not come up with a small trick to challenge her? Everyone said yes. Kang then asked for paper and pen and wrote the eight characters "司月二大旦午住了" (si yue er da dan wu zhu le). He asked the bride to add a stroke to each character and then recite it to the guests again. After a while, the characters had been added, and the bride's cheeks were flushed, and she refused to recite it. Everyone was surprised and asked for the paper to look at it. It turned out to be the eight characters "同用工夫早生佳子" (tong yong gong fu zao sheng jia zi), meaning "Work hard together and have good children early." Everyone laughed and stopped.

▲ Today, Mr. Yao Suifeng's novel "Women, Women" will be suspended for one day.

Travel Notes of India (85) 179

— Linghua

On the tenth day, I visited the monk Shenxin in a garden. Kapok flowers were in full bloom. This tree is only found in Guangdong and Guangxi. It is tall and has no branches or leaves. The flowers are red and large. There is also a tree similar to a weeping willow, with long branches and large leaves. This garden belongs to a wealthy family, and it is their duty to support monks. They have four meals a day, breaking the rule of not eating after noon. Moreover, Shenxin has traveled in Europe and America for a long time, and he is indeed a new monk, as Master Taixu said. However, I think this new monk is too studious, and his eyesight is very poor, but he still does not let go of his books all day long. He is currently reading Gandhi's autobiography. I have introduced the first volume of this biography. Now, I have glanced at the two thick volumes of the second volume. The thickness of the second volume is even greater than that of the first volume. I can't look at it in detail. I am not a worm in the book and do not want to see too many paintings. His autobiography repeatedly mentions the book Geta, a classic of Hinduism. It also mentions the experience of light diet and hygiene, which is roughly the same as the purpose of the coarse food and health method I wrote in previous years. However, there is no good way to deal with the conflict between the law of protecting cows by Indians and the killing of cows by Muslims. I think deeply about it, and there is no good way either. The issue of cows is indeed difficult to resolve. However, I think that the morality of Indians is commendable, and this is the point. I really believe that human nature is not as good as that of cows. It is difficult to say that human beings have conscience. The Indian people have conscience. Gandhi's autobiography concludes with God, which is beyond my knowledge. In short, Gandhi is the leader of the Brahmin sect, more than Tolstoy, who is the leader of the new Christian sect. In the evening, when the sun was setting, I followed the monk to the back garden, which is on the Ganges River. The monk's eyesight is very short, and his feet are not good. He went down to the river embankment, supporting my shoulder. The Indians were surprised to see a Chinese person supporting an Indian monk. I came to worship the Buddha without a Buddha. The Indian monk is the representative of the Buddha. I am very happy to worship him. I cannot believe that God is real. I also do not believe that God helps good people, but I am close to people of all religions and follow their habits. I do not believe in any kind of religion, but I believe that he is a human being. Therefore, I also respect what he respects. Small boats travel back and forth in the river, and many middle-aged and elderly women come to worship the Ganges water. When they see the monks, they all raise their hands to salute. Indian ships are similar to Chinese ships, but when I think of the dangers and thieves on ships in the Yangtze River and other places in Shanghai, I am frightened. There are too many thief boats in China. Only the boats in Guangdong are mainly run by women, and I feel quite safe. When I returned to the school, I saw groups of cows entering and leaving the school. All schools in India have cows. Cows are gods and public milk mothers. There are conscientious human beings in the world, only the Indian people. Indian culture is the culture of white cows. Therefore, it is appropriate for cows to enter and leave the university.

Yesterday, in the foreign firm tea market of this port, there were no major transactions in red and green box teas from various routes. The existing stock of green tea such as Precious Eyebrow and major gangs on the current market is no more than 10,000 to 20,000 boxes. In reality, there is already a situation where supply cannot meet demand. Chinese tea merchants are not selling goods in their hands until the price rises. Therefore, yesterday's transactions in various teas were scarce, and tea prices remained firm.

Piece Goods: Winter Goods and Woolens Pour In, Over 6,000 Boxes 196

The woolen goods and woolens sold in winter have gradually poured in recently. The goods shipped in April, May and June are all successively imported. Among them, those shipped by Italian, French, British and Japanese mail ships account for the most, with Qi Zhan in the east and west of the Huangpu River. Overcoats and velvets, as well as real and fake horse palm sleeves, melton, etc., are the most numerous. French shirts, fancy foreign cloths,

Hardware North Merchants Actively Purchasing Hardware 197

Hardware transactions have been very slow recently, mainly because various regions have been affected by floods, resulting in little demand. Therefore, the overall market trend is quite quiet. However, merchants from the north, such as Harbin, Niuzhuang, and Yingkou, have recently boycotted Eastern goods, so they have come to Shanghai to purchase European and American goods. As a result, the business of merchants from other places in Shanghai is slightly more active than before. According to market reports yesterday, the goods sold included 650 boxes of tinplate, priced at sixteen taels and two mace and five candareens for 90 pounds of American goods, and seventeen taels and two mace and five candareens for 100 pounds; British goods were priced at fourteen taels and five mace for 90 pounds, and fifteen taels and five mace for 100 pounds; 740 bundles of black iron sheet, priced at eleven taels and two mace and five candareens; 200 barrels of French and Spanish nails, priced at eight taels and eight mace and five candareens; 190 bundles of American white iron, with prices remaining unchanged from before. There was also some demand for British steel plates, angle iron, new silver dollars, and fire-treated wire, but the quantities were quite small.

Society News

Antiquities and Treasures of the Java Museum 214

— Ai Qing

Impressions of Java, IV

Museums in semi-civilized nations are often overlooked by antique enthusiasts in civilized countries. After Java's subjugation, items rarely seen among the populace were moved by the Dutch government to the museum for display. Furthermore, historical and artistically valuable antiquities from various civilized nations are interspersed within, with various treasures and antiques categorized and placed in separate exhibit rooms for visitors to appreciate at will.

The most numerous exhibits are the treasures and exotic pearls of the Javanese royal palace, including the royal swords used by kings from five hundred years ago. Legend has it that the swords were for the exclusive use of the kings to pass down to their descendants. Others have myths about the pommels. The sword hilts, scabbards, and sword sheaths are all inlaid with hundreds of diamonds of various sizes, radiating brilliance and making it difficult to look at them for long. One ancient crown is about a foot tall and weighs seven pounds, cast from red gold and inlaid with gemstones and pearls. According to gem merchants, one crown in the museum is worth over a million Dutch guilders. In the queen's treasure chest, there are diamonds, agates, ambers, pearls, and various other jewels the size of wine cups, each with its own brilliant light, leaving visitors to exclaim in admiration. It is truly not an exaggeration to say that the Southern Seas are a land of pearls.

In another exhibition room, historical royal robes, imperial concubine clothing, court attire, iron armor, battle robes, spears, and other weapons made of wood and stone are displayed. There are also royal robes woven from bark and coconut leaves hundreds of years ago. These relics easily evoke memories of our nation's material culture from thousands of years ago.

The museum is about one-third full of coins, sculptures, weavings, porcelain, and pottery from various countries and eras. There are also Chinese coins and porcelain from the Han and Tang dynasties on display. Visitors to the museum can feast their eyes.

It is now said that the Dutch government plans to expand the museum and intends to invite archaeological experts to specialize in purchasing antiques and treasures from Europe, America, and various countries in the Far East to add to the museum's exhibits. Perhaps in the future, it will not fall behind the museums of civilized nations.

Recent Mussolini 215

— Translated by Gao Zongyuan

Today's Mussolini and the Mussolini of the early Fascist era are almost like two different people.

The charm of the Italian Prime Minister Mussolini may be more renowned in the world than that of even the most celebrated silver screen star in Hollywood. At the mention of Mussolini's name, the average person will envision a composite image of Napoleon, Caesar, and a hypnotist trying to lull a stubborn patient to sleep: a pair of eyes with a bronze-like gaze, a face with a haughty and angry expression, and an air of arrogance and boldness. These can be considered the prominent features of this image. However, no matter how accurately you depict Mussolini's appearance from a few years ago, today's Mussolini is vastly different from the Mussolini of the past. Frankly speaking, since assuming national power for eight or nine years, Mussolini has softened considerably. The sharp edges have long been gradually worn away by frequent diplomacy. His outlook on life differs from that of ordinary people; he views life from the perspective of someone who commands the masses. Consequently, his appearance has been affected, and his demeanor has gradually become milder. Now, his stature has also greatly increased.

His attainment of today's position is due to revolution. Eight years ago, he was a revolutionary leader, not only in fact but also in the organization of his mind, in his biased aversion to things at the time, and in his eagerness for reform, change, development, and improvement. Now, eight years have passed, fleetingly gone, and eight years of meritorious service have followed, leaving only their traces behind.

Mussolini's physiological characteristics have perhaps changed the least. He still has those slightly protruding, piercing eyes, his uneven gums, and his arrogant demeanor. I saw an old photograph of Mussolini a long time ago, a family portrait taken after his first child was born. I suppose it was eighteen or nineteen years ago. The photograph showed his wife sitting, holding a baby named Edda, and Mussolini standing behind her. At that time, he was just an obscure editor of a socialist newspaper called Avanti!, more familiar with the arduous life of literary work than with the position of a dictator.

However, his appearance, his protruding chin, his Napoleonic demeanor, and the expression he shows now when reviewing the Fascist militia or when receiving the cheers of the adoring masses are no different. His condescending and awe-inspiring air is clearly natural and not something he feigns. What has changed is not his eyes, but the light that emanates from them.

Many people who meet Mussolini for the first time are often surprised at how such a figure can be as courteous as an ordinary person. This is because the common perception of Mussolini as an arrogant figure is deeply ingrained in their minds. When they sense that he is full of all human kindness, that he can joke and make people happy, that he can sympathize with others, that he does not ruthlessly dismiss others' opinions, and that he is happy to seek their advice—in other words, that he is a reasonable person—they find it even stranger.

Anyone who comes to seek an audience and is led into his famous office, the Hall of Triumph, is mostly prepared to endure a severe ordeal, that is, to pass through that grand room under his tightly furrowed brow and piercing cold gaze. People have talked a lot about this chilling feeling, and many articles have been written about it. So, people had anticipated it beforehand. But now, the situation is the opposite of what it was before. In any case, the people who came to visit were generally greeted at the door by a short, stout man wearing an immaculate, spotless morning suit, striped trousers, and a flower carefully placed in his buttonhole. He graciously extended a hand. As he accompanied them through the room and invited them to sit down, he smiled sincerely. Initially, the visiting guests often couldn't believe that this affable host was the Mussolini they had long feared.

His conversations also do not proceed as people expect. He does not quietly sit behind his desk, constantly wearing the expression of a strict teacher scolding a naughty child, asking loud and sudden questions. He is very charming. He listens intently and constantly shows his intense interest in what the visitors have to say. He answers their questions very smartly and fluently.

A famous American painter who once sat for Mussolini praised him in my presence as one of the most courteous people he had ever met in his life.

Mussolini's transformation is most evident in his speeches. When he first took office, he was one of the most stubborn politicians in Europe and one of the most frequent speakers. He never missed an opportunity to speak. His speeches were generally known for their audacity and vehement language rather than for their profound meaning. His speeches could manage to hold the audience in breathless silence without using theory to convince them. He used threats more often than arguments. As time passed, his speeches gradually decreased. Now, his speeches are delivered after careful consideration, and their effect is based on principle rather than on flamboyant rhetoric. He has learned to speak only when there are important issues to address, and his speeches now receive the effect that they could not before.

Mussolini's style of speaking has not actually changed. His speeches often lack the elements that are most beloved by Italian speakers. He rarely uses beautiful phrases. He says what he wants to say in plain language that everyone can understand. He does not use convoluted sentences or difficult metaphors. As for body language, he uses even less. He does not wave his arms as ordinary Latin people are accustomed to doing, or rely on affectation to move people. He often uses his right hand to make a quick, vertical gesture to emphasize a point in his speech. It is extremely rare to see him pound the table to strengthen his argument. However, he generally achieves the effect he anticipates. He has a special attraction that can enchant his audience. He can make them ecstatic and enthusiastic to the extreme without using the flowery phrases or gorgeous metaphors that ordinary Italian speakers are accustomed to using.

When he speaks to the public in the open air, he exerts all his strength. His voice fills the largest space. He seems to have a full understanding of mass psychology. I have seen the vast open space in Bologna crowded with hundreds of thousands of people, and he has the ability to move them... He can make the audience enthusiastic to the point of intoxication, and he can make them as silent as the grave. A great man of an era who can control the emotions of the masses is truly amazing and truly admirable.

Mussolini is now very unlikely to speak in the open air. He often speaks to the Fascist militia or at meetings of key figures in the Fascist provincial party or in front of delegations of industry and commerce representatives, but these are almost all private gatherings in which ordinary people are not allowed to participate. He used to like to gather the masses under the window of his office, and he would shout to them from the balcony, where he almost lost his life when his predecessor, Senator Zaniboni, tried to shoot him from a nearby window with a rifle. He no longer does this. All his speeches of a political nature are delivered in the Senate, in the Cabinet, or in the private room of the Fascist Grand Council. In recent years, his speeches have become more measured in tone and have completely lost their previously distinctive features. Not long ago, when he was speaking to the key figures of the Fascist provincial party, who represented the Italian Fascist Party Headquarters, about four thousand people in total, he would have seized this as a God-given opportunity to launch a fierce attack on his opponents. However, he confined himself to making a rigorous critique of the achievements of the Fascist Party over the past eight years.

From a newly published collection of his speeches from the entire year of 1928, it can be seen that he made about forty speeches that year. Only two of them were of a political nature, and both were about foreign politics. One was delivered in the Cabinet, and the other was delivered in the Parliament. The rest were short speeches—often only a few words—delivered at the opening of Parliament, at the laying of the foundation stone of public buildings, at receptions, or at several similar ceremonies.

Marshal Foch's War Memoirs (European War) 216

— Translated by Gu Angruo

The Battle of Montdidier, August 8th to 12th, 1918

At four o'clock in the morning on August 8, 1918, amidst the fog that continued to envelop the preparations of the previous night, our artillery began a fierce bombardment, destroying the enemy's gun emplacements. The infantry and tanks of the British Fourth Army advanced from the trenches forty-five minutes after the bombardment.

Caught completely off guard by the intensity and speed of our attack, the enemy forces collapsed in extreme disarray, abandoning countless supplies. Our army advanced more than six miles that day, opening up a twelve-mile front. Our army secured a firm foothold on the Montdidier plateau, capturing 13,000 prisoners and 300 cannons. Now was the time to advance victoriously. Colonel Tidek was therefore ordered to transmit the following military message to General Debeney on the morning of the 9th:

You are certainly aware that the French First Army should advance as quickly as possible to link up with the Third Army at Roye. Once the link is established, the second step can be carried out according to the evolution of the situation. Precisely because we cannot definitively decide what action to take today, everything must be adapted to circumstances. Absolutely no division or corps of troops is allowed to be transferred to the rear. Should a troop be unable to advance further, it can be deployed in the second line for support. The march must be swift, using all available forces in the rear to screen and press forward to the front lines until the planned objective is reached. Only after this step is completed can all losses be avoided in a few days.

Shortly after, I saw that General Debeney encountered difficulties when his right wing crossed the Avre River south of Montdidier, so I sent him another order:

Since General Debeney has determined that the linchpin of his march is on the far side of Montdidier, it is imperative not to overlook it. The wing advancing along the Roye road on the right bank of the Avre River is the point of contact with the British army (i.e., the stronger army). He must personally command there, and especially pay attention to the 31st Regiment actively advancing towards Roye, where his heroes will find their place.

On the 9th, the Franco-British Allied forces made further significant progress. Seeing that they were surrounded on both the north and south sides, the enemy forces withdrew from Montdidier the following evening.

On the 10th, the offensive continued. North of the Somme River, around Bray, and to the south, around Chaulnes and Roye, many positions were captured.

The French Third Army, in turn, received orders from Commander Foch to join the battle. Since August 5th, he had anticipated that this offensive by the Franco-British Allied forces would be very advantageous, so he ordered the Third Army to prepare to participate in the battle on the right wing of the First Army. The Third Army moved towards Lassigny.

The Allied Commander then sent the following military order to the commanders of each army on the 10th:

1. The British Fourth Army and the French First Army continue to advance eastward towards Hem. The British army aims to reach the Somme River below Hem in preparation for crossing the river, while continuing to cross the river from the Bray area to Péronne. The French army will cover the British advance, with the Jusca - Hem road as the target.

2. The French Third Army is now advancing towards Lassigny-Noyon, closely following the French First Army to clear out the remaining enemy forces in the Montdidier and Noyon areas.

3. Marshal Haig should quickly prepare the British Third Army to operate towards Bapaume and Péronne to shake the enemy's defensive line and seize the opportunity to advance.

Our army advanced smoothly on the left bank of the Somme River, moving very quickly. Inevitably, there would be a day of pause, whether due to being out of breath or encountering obstacles in the face of strong enemy defenses, as it was necessary to deploy military forces on the right bank of the Somme River and in the Attois area so that they could engage in battle when the opportunity arose. Therefore, the tenth day's military order included a third section:

On the morning of the 10th, I visited Marshal Haig to explain the meaning of expanding the British army's operations north of the Somme River and towards Arras. In this way, our army's achievements would not be sacrificed due to local battles, and continuous victories could confuse the enemy's plans and fundamentally shake the enemy's resistance by delivering new blows to the enemy's weak points. This was even more beneficial to the Allied forces. These military operations should be prepared immediately.

But now, after three days of continuous attacks, the Franco-British Allied forces suddenly encountered stubborn resistance. The enemy had now reached the old positions of 1914 and seemed determined to defend them.

On August 11, the left wing of the British Fourth Army and the French First Army could no longer advance, except for some progress between the Avre and Somme rivers. Although the right wings of the French Third and First Armies made great progress towards Lassigny, it was of no avail.

I strongly urged Marshal Haig to actively advance towards Bray. On the evening of the 11th, I personally visited him to ask him to fight with all his strength again. But the next day, in a letter I sent to the two British and French commanders-in-chief, I explained that new tactics must be adopted to achieve our army's objectives between the Somme and Oise rivers, namely, to repel the enemy at the Somme River and to capture all the bridges at and below Hem. The content of the letter is as follows:

If the enemy stubbornly resists, our army must not advance simultaneously along the entire front. This strategy would weaken our entire line. Our army should concentrate its forces on several key points and strike forcefully—in other words, those points which, once captured, would cause the enemy to collapse. It is also necessary to disrupt the enemy's lines of communication. These military operations must be arranged quickly, and the forces most suitable for attacking fortifications, such as tanks, artillery, and infantry, must be mobilized.

The steps of the operation are as follows:

(A) The right wings of the French First Army and the British Fourth Army should join forces to attack as quickly as possible, with the aim of capturing the road network around Roye. The French Third Army should cover the south with the aim of clearing the Noyon area.

(B) Without delay, the center of the British Fourth Army should advance northwest from the vicinity of Leschelles, with the aim of capturing the Amiens-Cambrai road. At the very least, that road must be within range of field artillery fire. The left wing of the British Fourth Army should assist from the east.

To expand the scope of our army's offensive, I added the following point:

Expanding the attack to both wings—north of the Somme River and east of the Oise River—can increase the gains. The plan is as follows: (To be continued)

Publishing News 217

▲The Great China Book Company, located in Yulin Lane, Guling Road, announces that the bookstore recruits very few people with achievements in national literature. However, this type of book is an essential book for the academic community. In view of this, the bookstore has specially collected thousands of national language achievements from schools across the country, compiled and printed them into a book, named "Compilation of National Language Achievements". The content is complete, the exploration and extraction are appropriate, and party and state dignitaries are invited to inscribe the book. It is now available for pre-sale. The price is two yuan and forty cents, and the pre-sale price is half price, one yuan and twenty cents, and so on.

▲Tan Yunshan's Letter Receiving Office announces that the calligrapher Tan Yunshan has donated a total of 1,000 pieces of calligraphy, including couplets, hall scrolls, hanging scrolls, and fan faces. Each piece costs one yuan for ink in this city, and one yuan and a half outside the city. In recent days, people from all walks of life who request Tan's calligraphy have flocked to the office, and the receiving office is almost overwhelmed. In the past ten days, more than 300 letters have been received. Tan wields his brush from morning to night every day, without any sense of fatigue. It is heard that the remaining amount of his donation is limited. If people at home and abroad admire Tan's calligraphy, please send the letters to Peng Qizhi, Taotao Restaurant, East Wuchang Road, Hongkou, who will forward them. It will take about a week to pick up the pieces, and so on.

Medical News 218

▲Ms. Qian Shuzhen, the daughter of the painter Qian Huafo, has set up a clinic at the intersection of Sanma Road and Yunnan Road, and the clinic business has been very prosperous. Last month, she was invited to Wuxi by a wealthy gentleman named Qin to assist in childbirth. She has now returned to Shanghai. Because the original clinic is insufficient, she has added a branch clinic at No. 778, Qingyuli, New Chongqing Road, and has hired several experienced female obstetricians to assist her.

▲The Shanghai New Hospital, opposite the Central Grand Theatre on Sixma Road, announces that because the hospital has been busy with clinic business due to the change of seasons between summer and autumn, it has specially hired Dr. Zhong Dingshen from Germany to preside over the clinic business. Dr. Zhong has extensive experience in medicine and is particularly cautious in clinical practice. During the Northern Expedition of the Party Army, he served as a military doctor in various armies and achieved considerable results. He is particularly proficient in the department of venereal diseases. In recent years, many people in Shanghai have been cured by him. He is now scheduled to see patients at the hospital every day from 2 pm to 6 pm. The consultation fee is only one yuan and twenty cents to show consideration for poor families.

Theater News 219

The Fuan Grand Theatre, opposite Xiaodongmen, announces that the theatre has been screening famous Chinese and foreign films and has been praised by all walks of life as the most beautiful and elegant entertainment venue in the urban area. In addition to paying attention to the selection and screening of famous films, the managers of the theatre have also meticulously decorated the tea service, reception, and interior furnishings. Starting yesterday, the Silver Star Troupe will perform "Red and Green Eyes," which is still the first of its kind in Shanghai.
